<p style="margin-left: 0.5in; text-indent: -0.5in;"><span style="font-size: 18pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">The First Step of the Aspirant by Swami Krishnananda</span></b></span></p>
</div>
<p style="text-align: justify;"><strong><span style="font-family: book antiqua,palatino; font-size: 12pt; color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;">Baba Times Digest© | 11 April 2014 15:29 EST | New York Edition</span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><span style="color: #0000ff;"></span></span></span><span style="color: #3366ff;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"><br /></span></span></strong></p>

<td style="padding: 0in 9pt;" align="left" valign="top"><!--[if gte mso 9]><xml>

<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>The First Step of the Aspirant<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" align="center" style="text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Divine Life Society Publication: - </b><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/realis/realis_8.html"><b>The Realisation of The Absolute</b></a><b> by Sri Swami Krishnananda<o:p></o:p></b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">Vedanta is the Science of Reality. Reality is uncontradicted experience, the experience that is not transcended or sublated by any other experience. Naturally, Reality must be imperish-able, for perishability marks a state or a thing as unreal. Imperishability means, at the same time, unlimitedness, for limit is non-independence and non-absoluteness, which means changefulness. Changelessness is the nature of Truth. The world which we live in is characterized by change and destruction. The world includes the individual, also. The body of an individual is a part of the world as a whole. The changing character of the world is kept up by changing events, changing actions, changing thoughts and feelings. Hence, the quest for Reality must necessarily be of a nature quite different from the natural ways of the world. The seeker after the Real has to be specially equipped with the power of separating Truth from falsehood; Reality from the unreal, transient universe.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The change required of an aspirant after the Real is not an ordinary external one, but a total transfiguration of life itself. This extraordinary change in life is hard to be had; the seeker after Perfection is asked to get himself ready for this great change for good.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The immediate reality which presents itself before us is the physical body situated in the physical world. Hence the first discipline required is of bodily actions or <i>karma</i>. <i>Karma</i> has a special significance in religion and philosophy. In addition to service devoid of individualistic motive or desire, <i>karma</i> means the selfless performance of one’s own prescribed duty without reluctance or failure. Every person is expected to be either a <i>brahmachari</i>, a <i>grihastha</i>, a <i>vanaprastha</i> or a <i>sannyasi</i>. One should not live, as far as it is within one’s capacity, in a stage which is not one of these four. And also, a person can belong to only one <i>ashrama</i> at a time, not to more than one. Performance of one’s own duty means the observance of the <i>ashrama-dharma</i>. <i>Nitya</i> and <i>naimittika</i> <i>karmas</i> pertaining to an <i>ashrama</i> constitute <i>svadharma</i> or one’s own duty, as far as the <i>Vedanta</i> philosophy is concerned with it. <i>Kamya-karmas</i> are excluded from <i>svadharma</i>.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The rigid observance of <i>svadharma</i> renders the mind pure (<i>shuddha</i>), freeing it from <i>mala</i>, the gross <i>tamas</i> and <i>rajas</i> which are the deluding and the distracting factors in it. The <i>Vedanta</i> prescribes <i>upasana</i> or the worship of and meditation on the personal God (<i>Saguna Brahman</i>) to those who have thus already purified their nature or attained <i>chitta-shuddhi</i> through <i>nishkama-karma</i>. <i>Upasana</i> removes <i>vikshepa</i> and brings <i>chitta-ekagrata</i> or one-pointedness of mind. It is this prepared aspirant who is qualified with <i>shuddhi</i> and <i>ekagrata</i> of <i>chitta</i> that is required to possess the <i>sadhana-chatushtaya</i>, the ethical requisites which are directly connected with the entrance to the main court of <i>Vedanta-sadhana</i>.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><i>Sadhana-chatushtaya</i> means the fourfold equipment, the necessary means to <i>brahma-vidya</i>, which removes <i>avarana</i> or the veil of ignorance. The discussion about the <i>adhikari</i> is one of the main subjects in the <i>Vedanta</i>. The first of these <i>sadhanas</i> is <i>viveka</i> or clear discrimination between the Eternal Principle and the perishable universe of names and forms. <i>Viveka</i> generally comes through <i>purva-punya</i> or the effect of past meritorious deeds accelerated by the perception of pain and death here. <i>Satsanga</i> is another factor which generates <i>viveka</i>. Perhaps <i>satsanga</i> is the greatest of all the means that transforms a person from worldliness to divine life. <i>Satsanga</i> leads to <i>viveka</i> and <i>vichara</i>, consciousness of the inadequacy of the phenomenal world and enquiry into the nature of Truth.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><i>Viveka</i> creates an indifference to the world and its contents. This supreme indifference born of <i>viveka</i> is the second of the four means, <i>vairagya</i>. True <i>vairagya</i> is the effect of correct discrimination and not of mere failure in life. Real dispassion is the consequence of the perception of the impermanence of things, the falsity of the existence of happiness in objects, the knowledge of the distinction between Reality and appearance. This <i>vairagya</i> reaches even up to <i>Brahmaloka</i>, the highest phenomenal manifestation, and discards it as defective. Thus, <i>vairagya</i> is distaste for everything that is objective (including one’s own body). It is not possible to love the Eternal as long as there is faith in the impermanent. Immortality and mortality are set against each other. Passion for the world and its objects is opposed to devotion to the Supreme Being, even as darkness is against light. Where the latter is, the former is not. <i>Vairagya</i> is the gateway to the knowledge of what truly is.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The third of the requisites is <i>shatsampat</i> or the sixfold wealth of internal discipline and virtues. (1) Tranquillity of mind (<i>shama</i>) which is the result of <i>viveka</i> and <i>vairagya</i>, (2) Self-restraint (<i>dama</i>) or control of the senses which is the effect of the knowledge of the ultimate worthlessness of the forms of external objects, (3) Cessation from distracting activity connected with the world (<i>uparati</i>), (4) Fortitude (<i>titiksha</i>) or the power to endure the ravages of Nature, like heat and cold, hunger and thirst, censure and praise, insult and injury, etc., (5) Faith (<i>shraddha</i>) in God, Preceptor, Scripture and the Voice of one’s own purified Conscience, and (6) One-pointedness of mind (<i>samadhana</i>), i.e., resting of the mind in the spiritual Ideal alone to the exclusion of everything else, are the six spiritual qualities which together make up the <i>shatsampat</i>. All these virtues are to be developed on the basis of correct understanding or clarified intelligence and not by mere force. The greater and more purified the understanding, the more precious and diviner is the virtue.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNoSpacing" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;">The last of the four means is <i>mumukshutva</i> or an ardent yearning for freeing oneself from the ignorance of finite life. These are the important conditions that are to be fulfilled by every aspirant after the Absolute Truth, before he actually starts <i>sadhana</i> in its strict sense. It is to be, however, pointed out again, that none of these <i>sadhanas</i> is to be practiced with brute force without proper purification and a brilliant discrimination.</span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span class="MsoHyperlink" style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b>Excerpts from:&nbsp;</b></span></p>
<p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 12pt; font-family: 'book antiqua', palatino;"><b style="text-align: center; line-height: 16.5px;"><span style="line-height: 115%;">The First Step of the Aspirant<span class="MsoHyperlink"> - </span></span></b><span style="text-align: center; line-height: 115%;"><a href="http://www.swami-krishnananda.org/realis/realis_8.html"><b><span style="line-height: 115%;">The Realisation of The Absolute</span></b></a></span><b style="text-align: center; line-height: 16.5px;"><span style="line-height: 115%;"> by Sri Swami Krishnananda</span></b></span></p>
